    </div>

      <div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">
       Indian national administrative subdivisions
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Not to be confused with <a href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_India" title="Administrative divisions of India">Administrative divisions of India</a>.
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       "Indian state" redirects here. It is not to be confused with <a href="/wiki/Indiana" title="Indiana">Indiana</a> or <a href="/wiki/Indian_Territory" title="Indian Territory">Indian Territory</a>.
      </div>

      <p><a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a> is a <a href="/wiki/Federalism" title="Federalism">federal</a> union comprising 28 <a href="/wiki/Federated_state" title="Federated state">states</a> and 8 <a href="/wiki/Union_territory" title="Union territory">union territories</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> for a total of 36 entities. The states and union territories are further subdivided into <a href="/wiki/List_of_districts_in_India" title="List of districts in India">districts</a> and smaller <a href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_India" title="Administrative divisions of India">administrative divisions</a>. </p> 
      <table class="vertical-navbox nowraplinks" style="float:right;clear:right;width:22.0em;margin:0 0 1.0em 1.0em;background:#f8f9fa;border:1px solid #aaa;padding:0.2em;border-spacing:0.4em 0;text-align:center;line-height:1.4em;font-size:88%">

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-independence">Pre-independence</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Presidencies_and_provinces_of_British_India" title="Presidencies and provinces of British India">Presidencies and provinces of British India</a>, <a href="/wiki/Agencies_of_British_India" title="Agencies of British India">Agencies of British India</a>, <a href="/wiki/Residencies_of_British_India" title="Residencies of British India">Residencies of British India</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Princely_state" title="Princely state">Princely state</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Indian_subcontinent" title="Indian subcontinent">Indian subcontinent</a> has been ruled by many different <a href="/wiki/South_Asian_ethnic_groups" title="South Asian ethnic groups">ethnic groups</a> throughout its history, each instituting their own policies of administrative division in the region.<sup id="cite_ref-Krishna_Reddy_2003_A107_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Krishna_Reddy_2003_A107-2">[2]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ramesh_Chandra_Majumdar_(1977)_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ramesh_Chandra_Majumdar_(1977)-3">[3]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Romila_Thapar_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Romila_Thapar-4">[4]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Grewal_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Grewal-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources#Bundling_citations" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This claim has too many footnotes for reading to be smooth. (July 2018)">excessive citations</span></a></i>]</sup> During the <a href="/wiki/British_Raj" title="British Raj">British Raj</a>, the preceding <a href="/wiki/Mughal_Empire" title="Mughal Empire">Mughal</a> administrative structure was mostly kept. India was divided into provinces (also called Presidencies) that were directly governed by the British and princely states which were nominally controlled by a local prince or raja loyal to the British Empire, which held <i><a href="/wiki/De_facto" title="De facto">de facto</a></i> sovereignty (<a href="/wiki/Suzerainty" title="Suzerainty">suzerainty</a>) over the princely states. </p> 
      <h3><span id="1947.E2.80.931950"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1947–1950">1947–1950</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Political_integration_of_India" title="Political integration of India">Political integration of India</a>, <a href="/wiki/Instrument_of_Accession" title="Instrument of Accession">Instrument of Accession</a>, <a href="/wiki/Annexation_of_Junagadh" title="Annexation of Junagadh">Annexation of Junagadh</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Annexation_of_Hyderabad" title="Annexation of Hyderabad">Annexation of Hyderabad</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Between 1947 and 1950 the territories of the princely states were politically integrated into the Indian Union. Most were merged into existing provinces; others were organised into new provinces, such as <a href="/wiki/Rajasthan" title="Rajasthan">Rajasthan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Himachal_Pradesh" title="Himachal Pradesh">Himachal Pradesh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Madhya_Bharat" title="Madhya Bharat">Madhya Bharat</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Vindhya_Pradesh" title="Vindhya Pradesh">Vindhya Pradesh</a>, made up of multiple princely states; a few, including <a href="/wiki/Mysore_State" title="Mysore State">Mysore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hyderabad_State_(1948%E2%80%9356)" class="mw-redirect" title="Hyderabad State (1948–56)">Hyderabad</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bhopal_State_(1949%E2%80%9356)" title="Bhopal State (1949–56)">Bhopal</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Bilaspur_State_(1950%E2%80%9354)" title="Bilaspur State (1950–54)">Bilaspur</a>, became separate provinces. The new <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_India" title="Constitution of India">Constitution of India</a>, which came into force on 26 January 1950, made India a sovereign democratic republic. The new republic was also declared to be a "Union of States".<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> The constitution of 1950 distinguished between three main types of states:<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <ul>
       <li>Part A states, which were the former governors' provinces of British India, were ruled by an elected governor and state legislature. The nine Part A states were <a href="/wiki/Assam" title="Assam">Assam</a> (formerly <a href="/wiki/Assam_Province" title="Assam Province">Assam Province</a>), <a href="/wiki/Bihar" title="Bihar">Bihar</a> (formerly <a href="/wiki/Bihar_Province" title="Bihar Province">Bihar Province</a>), <a href="/wiki/Bombay_State" title="Bombay State">Bombay</a> (formerly <a href="/wiki/Bombay_Presidency" title="Bombay Presidency">Bombay Province</a>), <a href="/wiki/East_Punjab" title="East Punjab">East Punjab</a> (formerly <a href="/wiki/Punjab_Province_(British_India)" title="Punjab Province (British India)">Punjab Province</a>), <a href="/wiki/Madhya_Pradesh" title="Madhya Pradesh">Madhya Pradesh</a> (formerly the <a href="/wiki/Central_Provinces_and_Berar" title="Central Provinces and Berar">Central Provinces and Berar</a>), <a href="/wiki/Madras_State" title="Madras State">Madras</a> (formerly <a href="/wiki/Madras_Presidency" title="Madras Presidency">Madras Province</a>), <a href="/wiki/Odisha" title="Odisha">Orissa</a> (formerly <a href="/wiki/Orissa_Province" title="Orissa Province">Orissa Province</a>), <a href="/wiki/Uttar_Pradesh" title="Uttar Pradesh">Uttar Pradesh</a> (formerly the <a href="/wiki/United_Provinces_(1937%E2%80%931950)" class="mw-redirect" title="United Provinces (1937–1950)">United Provinces</a>), and <a href="/wiki/West_Bengal" title="West Bengal">West Bengal</a> (formerly <a href="/wiki/Bengal_Presidency" title="Bengal Presidency">Bengal Province</a>).</li> 
       <li>The eight Part B states were former princely states or groups of princely states, governed by a <a href="/wiki/Rajpramukh" title="Rajpramukh">rajpramukh</a>, who was usually the ruler of a constituent state, and an elected legislature. The rajpramukh was appointed by the <a href="/wiki/President_of_India" title="President of India">President of India</a>. The Part B states were <a href="/wiki/Hyderabad_State_(1948%E2%80%9356)" class="mw-redirect" title="Hyderabad State (1948–56)">Hyderabad</a> (formerly <a href="/wiki/Hyderabad_State" title="Hyderabad State">Hyderabad Princely State</a>), <a href="/wiki/Jammu_and_Kashmir_(state)" title="Jammu and Kashmir (state)">Jammu and Kashmir</a> (formerly <a href="/wiki/Jammu_and_Kashmir_(princely_state)" title="Jammu and Kashmir (princely state)">Jammu and Kashmir Princely State</a>), <a href="/wiki/Madhya_Bharat" title="Madhya Bharat">Madhya Bharat</a> (formerly <a href="/wiki/Central_India_Agency" title="Central India Agency">Central India Agency</a>), <a href="/wiki/Mysore_State" title="Mysore State">Mysore</a> (formerly <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Mysore" title="Kingdom of Mysore">Mysore Princely State</a>), <a href="/wiki/Patiala_and_East_Punjab_States_Union" title="Patiala and East Punjab States Union">Patiala and East Punjab States Union</a> (PEPSU), <a href="/wiki/Rajasthan" title="Rajasthan">Rajasthan</a> (formerly <a href="/wiki/Rajputana_Agency" title="Rajputana Agency">Rajputana Agency</a>), <a href="/wiki/Saurashtra_(state)" title="Saurashtra (state)">Saurashtra</a> (formerly <a href="/wiki/Baroda,_Western_India_and_Gujarat_States_Agency" title="Baroda, Western India and Gujarat States Agency">Baroda, Western India and Gujarat States Agency</a>), and <a href="/wiki/Travancore-Cochin" class="mw-redirect" title="Travancore-Cochin">Travancore-Cochin</a> (formerly <a href="/wiki/Travancore" title="Travancore">Travancore Princely State</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Cochin" title="Kingdom of Cochin">Cochin Princely State</a>).</li> 
       <li>The ten Part C states included both the former chief commissioners' provinces and some princely states, and each was governed by a chief commissioner appointed by the President of India. The Part C states were <a href="/wiki/Ajmer_State" title="Ajmer State">Ajmer</a> (formerly <a href="/wiki/Ajmer-Merwara" title="Ajmer-Merwara">Ajmer-Merwara Province</a>), <a href="/wiki/Bhopal_State_(1949%E2%80%9356)" title="Bhopal State (1949–56)">Bhopal</a> (formerly <a href="/wiki/Bhopal_State" title="Bhopal State">Bhopal Princely State</a>), <a href="/wiki/Bilaspur_State_(1950%E2%80%9354)" title="Bilaspur State (1950–54)">Bilaspur</a> (formerly <a href="/wiki/Bilaspur_State_(princely_state)" title="Bilaspur State (princely state)">Bilaspur Princely State</a>), <a href="/wiki/Coorg_State" title="Coorg State">Coorg State</a> (formerly <a href="/wiki/Coorg_Province" title="Coorg Province">Coorg Province</a>), <a href="/wiki/Delhi" title="Delhi">Delhi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Himachal_Pradesh" title="Himachal Pradesh">Himachal Pradesh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kutch_State" title="Kutch State">Kutch</a> (formerly <a href="/wiki/Cutch_State" title="Cutch State">Cutch Princely State</a>), <a href="/wiki/Manipur" title="Manipur">Manipur</a> (formerly <a href="/wiki/Manipur_(princely_state)" title="Manipur (princely state)">Manipur Princely State</a>), <a href="/wiki/Tripura" title="Tripura">Tripura</a> (formerly <a href="/wiki/Tripura_(princely_state)" title="Tripura (princely state)">Tripura Princely State</a>), and <a href="/wiki/Vindhya_Pradesh" title="Vindhya Pradesh">Vindhya Pradesh</a> (formerly <a href="/wiki/Central_India_Agency" title="Central India Agency">Central India Agency</a>).</li> 
       <li>The only Part D state was the <a href="/wiki/Andaman_and_Nicobar_Islands" title="Andaman and Nicobar Islands">Andaman and Nicobar Islands</a>, which were administered by a lieutenant governor appointed by the union government.</li>
      </ul> 
      <h3><span id="States_reorganisation_.281951.E2.80.931956.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="States_reorganisation_(1951–1956)">States reorganisation (1951–1956)</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Goa_liberation_movement" title="Goa liberation movement">Goa liberation movement</a>, <a href="/wiki/Andhra_movement" title="Andhra movement">Andhra movement</a>, <a href="/wiki/Annexation_of_Dadra_and_Nagar_Haveli" title="Annexation of Dadra and Nagar Haveli">Annexation of Dadra and Nagar Haveli</a>, and <a href="/wiki/States_Reorganisation_Commission" title="States Reorganisation Commission">States Reorganisation Commission</a>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Andhra_State" title="Andhra State">Andhra State</a> was created on 1 October 1953 from the <a href="/wiki/Telugu_language" title="Telugu language">Telugu</a>-speaking northern <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_India" class="mw-redirect" title="Districts of India">districts</a> of <a href="/wiki/Madras_State" title="Madras State">Madras State</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Pondicherry" title="Pondicherry">Pondicherry</a>, comprising the previous <a href="/wiki/French_India" title="French India">French enclaves</a> of <a href="/wiki/Pondicherry_district" class="mw-redirect" title="Pondicherry district">Pondichéry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Karaikal_district" title="Karaikal district">Karikal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yanam_district" title="Yanam district">Yanaon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mah%C3%A9_district" class="mw-redirect" title="Mahé district">Mahé</a> was transferred to India in 1954 and became a union territory in 1962. The French enclave of <a href="/wiki/Chandannagar" title="Chandannagar">Chandernagore</a> was transferred to <a href="/wiki/West_Bengal" title="West Bengal">West Bengal</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the same year, pro-India forces liberated the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_India" title="Portuguese India">Portuguese-held enclaves</a> of <a href="/wiki/Dadra,_Dadra_and_Nagar_Haveli_and_Daman_and_Diu" title="Dadra, Dadra and Nagar Haveli and Daman and Diu">Dadrá</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nagar_Haveli" title="Nagar Haveli">Nagar Aveli</a>, declaring the short-lived <i><a href="/wiki/De_facto" title="De facto">de facto</a></i> state <a href="/wiki/Free_Dadra_and_Nagar_Haveli" title="Free Dadra and Nagar Haveli">Free Dadra and Nagar Haveli</a>. In 1961, it was annexed by India as the Union Territory of <a href="/wiki/Dadra_and_Nagar_Haveli" title="Dadra and Nagar Haveli">Dadra and Nagar Haveli</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/States_Reorganisation_Act,_1956" title="States Reorganisation Act, 1956">States Reorganisation Act, 1956</a> reorganised the states based on linguistic lines resulting in the creation of the new states.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> As a result of this act, <a href="/wiki/Madras_State" title="Madras State">Madras State</a> retained its name with <a href="/wiki/Kanyakumari_district" title="Kanyakumari district">Kanyakumari district</a> added to form <a href="/wiki/Travancore-Cochin" class="mw-redirect" title="Travancore-Cochin">Travancore-Cochin</a>. <a href="/wiki/Andhra_Pradesh" title="Andhra Pradesh">Andhra Pradesh</a> was created with the merger of <a href="/wiki/Andhra_State" title="Andhra State">Andhra State</a> with the Telugu-speaking districts of <a href="/wiki/Hyderabad_State" title="Hyderabad State">Hyderabad State</a> in 1956. <a href="/wiki/Kerala" title="Kerala">Kerala</a> was created with the merger of <a href="/wiki/Malabar_district" class="mw-redirect" title="Malabar district">Malabar district</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Kasaragod_taluk" title="Kasaragod taluk">Kasaragod taluk</a> of <a href="/wiki/South_Canara" title="South Canara">South Canara</a> districts of <a href="/wiki/Madras_State" title="Madras State">Madras State</a> with <a href="/wiki/Travancore-Cochin" class="mw-redirect" title="Travancore-Cochin">Travancore-Cochin</a>. <a href="/wiki/Mysore_State" title="Mysore State">Mysore State</a> was re-organized with the addition of districts of <a href="/wiki/Bellary_district" title="Bellary district">Bellary</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_Canara" title="South Canara">South Canara</a> (excluding <a href="/wiki/Kasaragod_taluk" title="Kasaragod taluk">Kasaragod taluk</a>) and the <a href="/wiki/Kollegal" title="Kollegal">Kollegal taluk</a> of <a href="/wiki/Coimbatore_district" title="Coimbatore district">Coimbatore district</a> from the Madras State, the districts of <a href="/wiki/Belgaum_district" class="mw-redirect" title="Belgaum district">Belgaum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bijapur_district,_Karnataka" title="Bijapur district, Karnataka">Bijapur</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Canara" class="mw-redirect" title="North Canara">North Canara</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dharwad_district" title="Dharwad district">Dharwad</a> from <a href="/wiki/Bombay_State" title="Bombay State">Bombay State</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Kannada" title="Kannada">Kannada</a>-majority districts of <a href="/wiki/Bidar_district" title="Bidar district">Bidar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Raichur_district" title="Raichur district">Raichur</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gulbarga_district" title="Gulbarga district">Gulbarga</a> from <a href="/wiki/Hyderabad_State_(1948%E2%80%9356)" class="mw-redirect" title="Hyderabad State (1948–56)">Hyderabad State</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Coorg_State" title="Coorg State">Coorg State</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Laccadive_Islands" title="Laccadive Islands">Laccadive Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aminidivi" title="Aminidivi">Aminidivi Islands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Minicoy" title="Minicoy">Minicoy Island</a> which were divided between South Canara and Malabar districts of Madras State were united and organised into the union territory of <a href="/wiki/Lakshadweep" title="Lakshadweep">Lakshadweep</a>. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Bombay_State" title="Bombay State">Bombay State</a> was enlarged by the addition of <a href="/wiki/Saurashtra_(state)" title="Saurashtra (state)">Saurashtra State</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kutch_State" title="Kutch State">Kutch State</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Marathi_language" title="Marathi language">Marathi</a>-speaking districts of <a href="/wiki/Nagpur_Division" class="mw-redirect" title="Nagpur Division">Nagpur Division</a> of <a href="/wiki/Madhya_Pradesh" title="Madhya Pradesh">Madhya Pradesh</a> and <a href="/wiki/Marathwada" title="Marathwada">Marathwada</a> region of <a href="/wiki/Hyderabad_State_(1948%E2%80%9356)" class="mw-redirect" title="Hyderabad State (1948–56)">Hyderabad State</a>. <a href="/wiki/Rajasthan" title="Rajasthan">Rajasthan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Punjab" title="Punjab">Punjab</a> gained territories from <a href="/wiki/Ajmer_State" title="Ajmer State">Ajmer State</a> and <a href="/wiki/Patiala_and_East_Punjab_States_Union" title="Patiala and East Punjab States Union">Patiala and East Punjab States Union</a> respectively and certain territories of <a href="/wiki/Bihar" title="Bihar">Bihar</a> was transferred to <a href="/wiki/West_Bengal" title="West Bengal">West Bengal</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-1956">Post-1956</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Mahagujarat_movement" title="Mahagujarat movement">Mahagujarat movement</a>, <a href="/wiki/Punjabi_Suba_movement" title="Punjabi Suba movement">Punjabi Suba movement</a>, <a href="/wiki/Annexation_of_Goa" title="Annexation of Goa">Annexation of Goa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Goa_Opinion_Poll" title="Goa Opinion Poll">Goa Opinion Poll</a>, <a href="/wiki/1975_Sikkimese_monarchy_referendum" title="1975 Sikkimese monarchy referendum">1975 Sikkimese monarchy referendum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Uttarakhand_movement" title="Uttarakhand movement">Uttarakhand movement</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Telangana_movement" title="Telangana movement">Telangana movement</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Bombay State was split into the linguistic states of <a href="/wiki/Gujarat" title="Gujarat">Gujarat</a> and <a href="/wiki/Maharashtra" title="Maharashtra">Maharashtra</a> on 1 May 1960 by the Bombay Reorganisation Act.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> Former Union Territory of <a href="/wiki/Nagaland" title="Nagaland">Nagaland</a> achieved statehood on 1 December 1963.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Punjab_Reorganisation_Act,_1966" title="Punjab Reorganisation Act, 1966">Punjab Reorganisation Act, 1966</a> resulted in the creation of <a href="/wiki/Haryana" title="Haryana">Haryana</a> on 1 November and the transfer of the northern districts of Punjab to <a href="/wiki/Himachal_Pradesh" title="Himachal Pradesh">Himachal Pradesh</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> The act also designated <a href="/wiki/Chandigarh" title="Chandigarh">Chandigarh</a> as a union territory and the shared capital of Punjab and Haryana.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Madras State was renamed <a href="/wiki/Tamil_Nadu" title="Tamil Nadu">Tamil Nadu</a> in 1969. North-eastern states of <a href="/wiki/Manipur" title="Manipur">Manipur</a>, <a href="/wiki/Meghalaya" title="Meghalaya">Meghalaya</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tripura" title="Tripura">Tripura</a> were formed on 21 January 1972.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> Mysore State was renamed as <a href="/wiki/Karnataka" title="Karnataka">Karnataka</a> in 1973. On 16 May 1975, <a href="/wiki/Sikkim" title="Sikkim">Sikkim</a> became the 22nd state of the Indian Union and the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Sikkim" title="Kingdom of Sikkim">state's monarchy</a> was abolished.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> In 1987, <a href="/wiki/Arunachal_Pradesh" title="Arunachal Pradesh">Arunachal Pradesh</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mizoram" title="Mizoram">Mizoram</a> became states on 20 February, followed by <a href="/wiki/Goa" title="Goa">Goa</a> on 30 May, while erstwhile union territory of <a href="/wiki/Goa,_Daman_and_Diu" title="Goa, Daman and Diu">Goa, Daman and Diu</a>'s northern <a href="/wiki/Exclave" class="mw-redirect" title="Exclave">exclaves</a> <a href="/wiki/Daman_district,_India" title="Daman district, India">Damão</a> and <a href="/wiki/Diu_district" title="Diu district">Diu</a> became separate union territory as <a href="/wiki/Daman_and_Diu" title="Daman and Diu">Daman and Diu</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In November 2000, three new states were created; namely, <a href="/wiki/Chhattisgarh" title="Chhattisgarh">Chhattisgarh</a> from eastern <a href="/wiki/Madhya_Pradesh" title="Madhya Pradesh">Madhya Pradesh</a>, Uttaranchal from northwest <a href="/wiki/Uttar_Pradesh" title="Uttar Pradesh">Uttar Pradesh</a> (renamed <a href="/wiki/Uttarakhand" title="Uttarakhand">Uttarakhand</a> in 2007) and <a href="/wiki/Jharkhand" title="Jharkhand">Jharkhand</a> from southern districts of Bihar with the enforcement of <a href="/wiki/Madhya_Pradesh_Reorganisation_Act,_2000" title="Madhya Pradesh Reorganisation Act, 2000">Madhya Pradesh Reorganisation Act, 2000</a>, <a href="/wiki/Uttar_Pradesh_Reorganisation_Act,_2000" title="Uttar Pradesh Reorganisation Act, 2000">Uttar Pradesh Reorganisation Act, 2000</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bihar_Reorganisation_Act,_2000" title="Bihar Reorganisation Act, 2000">Bihar Reorganisation Act, 2000</a> respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> Pondicherry was renamed as <a href="/wiki/Puducherry_(union_territory)" title="Puducherry (union territory)">Puducherry</a> in 2007 and Orissa was renamed as <a href="/wiki/Odisha" title="Odisha">Odisha</a> in 2011. <a href="/wiki/Telangana" title="Telangana">Telangana</a> was created on 2 June 2014 as ten former districts of north-western <a href="/wiki/Andhra_Pradesh" title="Andhra Pradesh">Andhra Pradesh</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In August 2019, the Parliament of India passed the <a href="/wiki/Jammu_and_Kashmir_Reorganisation_Act,_2019" title="Jammu and Kashmir Reorganisation Act, 2019">Jammu and Kashmir Reorganisation Act, 2019</a>, which contains provisions to reorganise the state of <a href="/wiki/Jammu_and_Kashmir_(state)" title="Jammu and Kashmir (state)">Jammu and Kashmir</a> into two union territories; <a href="/wiki/Jammu_and_Kashmir_(union_territory)" title="Jammu and Kashmir (union territory)">Jammu and Kashmir</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ladakh" title="Ladakh">Ladakh</a>, effective from 31 October 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> Later that year in November, the Government of India introduced legislation to merge the union territories of <a href="/wiki/Daman_and_Diu" title="Daman and Diu">Daman and Diu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dadra_and_Nagar_Haveli" title="Dadra and Nagar Haveli">Dadra and Nagar Haveli</a> into a single union territory to be known as <a href="/wiki/Dadra_and_Nagar_Haveli_and_Daman_and_Diu" title="Dadra and Nagar Haveli and Daman and Diu">Dadra and Nagar Haveli and Daman and Diu</a>, effective from 26 January 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Current_proposals">Current proposals</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Proposed_states_and_union_territories_of_India" title="Proposed states and union territories of India">Proposed states and union territories of India</a>
      </div>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Autonomous_areas">Autonomous areas</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_administrative_divisions_of_India" title="Autonomous administrative divisions of India">Autonomous administrative divisions of India</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The Sixth Schedule of the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_India" title="Constitution of India">Constitution of India</a> allows for the formation of <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_administrative_divisions_of_India" title="Autonomous administrative divisions of India">autonomous councils</a> to administer areas which have been given autonomy within their respective states.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[53]</a></sup> Most of these autonomous areas are located in <a href="/wiki/Northeast_India" title="Northeast India">Northeast India</a>. </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Responsibilities_and_authorities">Responsibilities and authorities</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Federalism_in_India" title="Federalism in India">Federalism in India</a>, <a href="/wiki/Union_List" title="Union List">Union List</a>, <a href="/wiki/State_List" title="State List">State List</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Concurrent_List" title="Concurrent List">Concurrent List</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_India" title="Constitution of India">Constitution of India</a> distributes the sovereign executive and legislative powers exercisable with respect to the territory of any State between the Union and that State.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[54]</a></sup> </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span></h2> 
      <div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;"> 
       <div class="mw-references-wrap">
        <ol class="references"> 
         <li id="cite_note-fn2-46"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-fn2_46-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Khasi language has been declared as the Additional Official Language for all purposes in the District, Sub-Division and Block level offices of the State Government located in the Districts of Khasi-Jaintia Hills of Meghalaya.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-fn1-47"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-fn1_47-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Andhra Pradesh was divided into two states, <a href="/wiki/Telangana" title="Telangana">Telangana</a> and a residual <a href="/wiki/Andhra_Pradesh" title="Andhra Pradesh">Andhra Pradesh</a> on 2 June 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Times_of_India_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Times_of_India-58">[55]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-APGazetteMar1_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-APGazetteMar1-59">[56]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-APGazetteMar4_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-APGazetteMar4-60">[57]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hyderabad,_India" class="mw-redirect" title="Hyderabad, India">Hyderabad</a>, located entirely within the borders of Telangana, is to serve as the capital for both states for a period of time not exceeding ten years.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[58]</a></sup> The Government of Andhra Pradesh and the Andhra Pradesh Legislature completed the process of relocating to temporary facilities in the envisaged new capital city <a href="/wiki/Amaravati" title="Amaravati">Amaravati</a> in early 2017.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-fn3-52"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-fn3_52-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Bengali and Nepali are the Official Languages in Darjeeling and Kurseong sub-divisions of Darjeeling district.</span> </li> 
        </ol>
       </div>
      </div>

         <li id="cite_note-57"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-57">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">"Article 73 broadly stated, provides that the executive power of the Union shall extend to the matters with respect to which Parliament has power to make laws. Article 162 similarly provides that the executive power of a State shall extend to the matters with respect to which the Legislature of a State has power to make laws. The Supreme Court has reiterated this position when it ruled in the <i>Ramanaiah case</i> that the executive power of the Union or of the State broadly speaking, is <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/coextensive" class="extiw" title="wikt:coextensive">coextensive</a> and <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/coterminous" class="extiw" title="wikt:coterminous">coterminous</a> with its respective legislative power." <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.ebc-india.com/lawyer/articles/9801a2.htm">Territoriality of executive powers of states in India</a>, Balwant Singh Malik, <i>Constitutional Law</i>, 1998</span> </li>
